Comment

This curious piece of prose is (with the exception of paragraphs here and there) found also in P─Бipp. xvi. тМКP─Бipp. has the order 22, 24, 23, 26, 25.тМЛ тМКThis is the first of the pary─Бya-s┼лktas. For the pary─Бya-hymns in general, see introduction to book viii., pages 471-2, above.тМЛ

тМКNeither K─Бu┼Ы. nor V─Бit. makes use of the hymn; but one of the “committals” in the upanayana (K─Бu┼Ы. 56. 13) is to m─Бrtyuс╣Бjaya m─Бrtyava: cf. vs. 23.тМЛ

Translation
  1. Vir─Б╠Бj verily was this [universe] in the beginning; of her when
    born everything was afraid, [thinking] “this one indeed will become
    this [universe].”
Notes

Ppp. reads тАШj─Бyata for ─Бs─лt, and, after tasy─Бs, j─Бt─Бy─Б тАЩbibhed eka
sarvam: yam eve тАЩdam bhaviс╣гyati na vayam iti.

Griffith

Viraj at first was This. At birth all feared her; the thought, She will become this All, struck terror.

She rose, she came unto the tress: they killed her. A year went by and she again existed. Hence in a year the wounds of trees heal over. He who knows this sees his loathed rival wounded.

Griffith

She mounted up, she came unto the Fathers: they killed her: in a month she re-existed. Hence men give monthly offerings to the Fathers: who knows this, knows the path which they have trodden.

Griffith

She rose, she came unto the Gods: they killed her: but in a fortnight she again was living. Fortnightly, hence, men serve the Gods with Vasat! Who knows this knows the way which Gods pass over.

Translation
  1. She ascended; she came to men (manuс╣гy├а); men slew her; she at once
    (sady├бs) came into being; therefore on both days they present
    (upa-hс╣Ы) to men; in his house do they present who knoweth thus.
Notes

‘Present,’ i.e. ‘food’; ‘on both days’ is a queer expression for ’every
day.’ Ppp. is corrupt, but perhaps means ahar-ahar manuс╣гy─Бс╣З─Бm upa h-.

[Pary─Бyas IV. and V.тАФdve с╣гoс╕Нa┼Ыake. a of 22, 23, 26, 29. 4-p.
s─Бmn─л jagat─л; b of 22-24, 28, 29. s─Бmn─л bс╣Ыhat─л; c of 22, 26.
s─Бmny uс╣гс╣Зih; d of 22, 23, 26, 29. ─Бrcy anuс╣гс╣нubh; c of 23. ─Бsur─л
g─Бyatr─л; a of 24, 25, 28. 4-p. uс╣гс╣Зih; c of 24. pr─Бj─Бpaty─Б
тАЩnuс╣гс╣нubh; d of 24, 25, 27. ─Бrc─л triс╣гс╣нubh; b of 25, 26. s─Бmny
uс╣гс╣Зih; c of 25, 27, 28. vir─Бс╕Н g─Бyatr─л; a of 27. 4-p. pr─Бj─Бpaty─Б
jagat─л; b of 27. s─Бmn─л triс╣гс╣нubh; d of 28. 3-p. br─Бhm─л bhurig
g─Бyatr─л; c of 29. s─Бmny anuс╣гс╣нubh.]

Griffith

She mounted up, she came to men: they killed her Presently she regained her life and being. Hence on both days to men they bring and offer–who knows this–near-seated in the dwelling.

  1. She ascended; she came to the Asuras; the Asuras called to her: O
    illusion (m─Бy─Б╠Б), come! of her Virochana son of Prahr─Бda was young
    (vats├б), the metal-(├бyas-)vessel [was] vessel; her Dvim┼лrdhan son
    of с╣Ъitu milked; from her he milked illusion; that illusion the Asuras
    subsist upon; one to be subsisted on becometh he who knoweth thus.
Notes

R. alone gives the first phrase in ┬з┬з22-28. In this and the following
paragraphs to 29 inclusive, the text should accent ─Б╠Бs─лt, with all the
mss. Ppp. reads v─Бirocanas instead of vir-. Single points in these
paragraphs find correspondences in MS. iv. (p. 21, l. 14 ff.; p. 36, l.
8 ff.) and in TB. ii. 2. 9тБ╢ ff. тМКcf. i. 5. 9┬▓тМЛ.

Griffith

She rose, approached the Asuras: they called her: their cry was, Come, O Maya, come thou hither. Her dear calf was Virochana Prahradi: her milking vessel was a. pan of iron. Dvimurdha Artvya milked her, yea, this Maya, The Asuras depend for life on Maya. He who knows this becomes a fit supporter.

Griffith

She mounted up, she came to men. They called her, Come unto- us, come hither thou Free-giver! Earth was her milking-pail, the calf beside her Manu Vaivasvata, Vivasvan’s offspring. Griffith

She rose approached the Apsarases and Gandharvas. They called her, Come to us, O Fragrant-scented! The son of Suryavarchas, Chitraratha, was her dear calf, her pail. a lotus-petal. The son of Suryavarchas, Vasuruchi, milked and drew from her most delightful fragrance. That scent supports Apsarases and Gandharvas. He who knows this becomes a meet supporter, and round him ever breathes delicious odour.

Griffith

She mounted up, she came unto the Serpents. The Serpents called her, Venomous! come hither. Her calf was Takshaka, Visala’s offspring: a bottlegourd suppli- ed a milking-vessel. Iravan’s offspring, Dhritarashtra milked her, and from her udder drew forth only poison. That poison quickens and supports the Serpents: He who knows this becomes a meet supporter.

  1. Then for whomsoever that knoweth thus one shall pour out with a
    gourd, he should reject [it].

Ppp. in this division of the hymn are “confused but apparently
essentially accordant” with those of our text. Read t├бd for y├бd at
the beginning in our text.

One would ward off, for him who hath this knowledge, if with a bottle-gourd he sprinkled water.

тМКThe quotations from the Old Anukr. for the pary─Бya-s┼лkta are given
piecemeal at the end of each pary─Бya. For brevity they may here be

с╣гoс╕Н┼Ыa; V. с╣гoс╕Нa┼Ыa; VI. catuс╣гkas.тМЛ

тМКSPP., “Critical Notice,” vol. i., p. 19, prints them in full in their

trayoda┼Ыa da┼Ы─Б тАЩс╣гс╣н─Бu ca tataс╕е с╣гoс╕Нa┼Ыa с╣гoс╕Нa┼Ыa:

‘In the [hymn beginning] “vir─Бс╕Н v─Б” (v─Бi), [the last pary─Бya
is] one of four [avas─Бna-rcas]; while the pary─Бyas count six.’]

[The summations of gaс╣Зas and (gaс╣Зa-)avas─Бna-rcas are as follows:

тМКHere ends the fifth anuv─Бka, with 2 hymns and 59 verses: that is 1
artha-s┼лkta of 26 verses and 1 pary─Бya-s┼лkta with 6 pary─Бyas and

тМКSome mss. sum up the hymns and verses correctly. Thus D. reckons 30
s┼лktas (that is 24 of the decad-divisions of our hymns 1-9, plus 6

plus 67 avas─Бna-rcas. Similarly ms. l. makes 30 hymns; but 259 verses

тМКHere ends the nineteenth prap─Бс╣нhaka.тМЛ
